- Powered Wheels (Blocks 109–120): Decorative only; do not bind or press any inputs; allow auto-brake; axes along ±x.

- Torches (Blocks 133–144): Lit; flames upward/outward; maintained ≥0.5 clearance to all wood/cannons.

Notes on single-piece integrity and safety
- All components remain one rigid sub-structure; no separations after assembly.
- Deck is 3×13 with six bearing feet at y=±6 to rest on terrain edges.
- Connectors attach only between free faces of existing blocks; no connector-to-connector attachments.
- If minor interference occurs during build, adjust a cannon’s inward cant or swap torch/cannon on that bay while preserving the even/odd alternation and y=0 omission.

# builder (gpt-5) (ThoughtEvent): 

Tooling overview and how we’ll use them step by step

I have the following tools available in this build simulation. Please note that every action adds exactly one block or modifies one existing block, and I will only make one tool call per message so we can build safely and verify as we go. Also, the note argument on many tools is very important: I will use it to tag each block/connection with its intended function (e.g., “Center row (0,+1,0)” or “East top-chord y=−6→−5”) so we can reliably identify and audit the structure later.

Available tools
- functions.start
  - Purpose: Create the initial starting block and place it in the world with a given shift and rotation.
  - Inputs needed: init_shift [x,y,z], init_rotation [yaw,pitch,roll] (optional), note (what we’re building).
  - Typical use here: Place the default Stone base at (0,0,0) to serve as Block 0.
- functions.attach_block_to
  - Purpose: Attach a new block directly to a specific face of an existing block.
  - Available new_block types: "Powered Wheel", "Small Wooden Block", "Torch", "Water Cannon".
  - Inputs needed: base_block (ID of existing block), face (the labeled face to attach to, e.g., North/South/East/West/Top/Bottom—captions can be confirmed with get_block_details), new_block (type to attach), note (critical for identification).
  - Notes: Faces are oriented to the global axes (east +x, north +y, up +z). This is the primary tool to add most of the blocks in your blueprint.
- functions.connect_blocks
  - Purpose: Connect two existing blocks by a connector element.
  - Connectors: "Brace" or "Winch".
  - Inputs needed: block_a, face_a, block_b, face_b, connector, note.
  - Notes: The connection will fail if faces are too close or invalid. I will choose the exact faces per the blueprint (e.g., “north face of Block 46 to south face of Block 50”). This places one connector per call.
- functions.get_block_details
  - Purpose: Retrieve full position/rotation/face info of a block.
  - Inputs needed: block_id.
  - Notes: I’ll use this when we need to confirm face names, orientation for wheels/cannons/torches, or to troubleshoot clearances.
- functions.shift_block
  - Purpose: Slightly adjust a block’s position (range per axis −0.5 to +0.5) after attachment, useful for minor interference.
  - Inputs needed: block_id, shift_real [dx,dy,dz].
  - Notes: If minor interference occurs (e.g., a post ornament contacts a torch), we can apply a small offset as your notes allow, while preserving alternating patterns.
- functions.twist_block
  - Purpose: Twist a block around its rooted surface by a given angle (degrees).
  - Inputs needed: block_id, angle.
  - Notes: Helpful for orienting Powered Wheels (axis along ±x) and aiming Water Cannons slightly inward/upward, or pointing Torch flames outward/upward.
- functions.flip_spin
  - Purpose: Flip the spin direction of a block that spins (e.g., a Powered Wheel).
  - Inputs needed: block_id.
  - Notes: Decorative wheels will remain unbound; we’ll ensure their axes are correct, but spin direction flips aren’t necessary since they’re decorative only.
- functions.remove_block
  - Purpose: Remove a block if we need to correct a mistake.
  - Inputs needed: block_id.
- functions.reset
  - Purpose: Reset the entire build to empty.
  - Inputs needed: none.
- functions.get_machine_summary
  - Purpose: Get the latest state overview of the whole build (without face captions). I will always use this for a final check before we end the process and will remind you before doing so.

Build approach for your Ornate Through-Truss Bridge (Single-Piece, 3×13 Deck)
- We will:
  1) Place the starting stone base at (0,0,0) as Block 0.
  2) Lay the center deck row northward then southward (Blocks 1–12).
  3) Add edge deck rows at x=±1 (Blocks 13–38).
  4) Add bearing feet at y=±6 (Blocks 39–44).
  5) Build parapet posts two-high on edge deck blocks (Blocks 45–96), skipping y=0 fixtures as specified for headroom.
  6) Install underhung medallion bases (Blocks 97–108).
  7) Attach Powered Wheels (Blocks 109–120) with correct axis along ±x; no controls bound.
  8) Mount Water Cannons and Torches on alternating z=+2 posts, skipping y=0 per your spec (Blocks 121–144), adjusting orientation to be upward and slightly inward (cannons) and upward/outward (torches) with clearance.
  9) Build the central pylon and cross-beam (Blocks 145–149).
  10) Add decorative Winches (Blocks 150–155).
  11) Add Braces for top-chords, side-panel diagonals, and portals (Blocks 156–194).
- Throughout, I’ll use the note field to label each placed block/connector precisely, and will verify/adjust orientation with twist_block as required for torches and cannons to ensure clearance and the specified alternation.
